03/10/24, 11:02 pm - +91 79874 18684: Dear Sir/Madam,

Greetings from the Ministry of Education’s Innovation Cell and AICTE.

The Smart India Hackathon (SIH) 2024 has kicked off with a bang, setting new records and showcasing India's innovative potential. The initial submission phase of the event has concluded, with a surge in participation and a remarkable display of creativity.

A total of 2,600 Higher Education Institutions (HEIs) took part in SIH 2024, organizing 2,171 internal hackathons. This led to the nomination of 49,237 teams, demonstrating the growing enthusiasm and interest in innovation among India's youth.

The participants showcased their problem-solving skills and entrepreneurial spirit by submitting 55,795 ideas. These ideas address a wide range of challenges, from healthcare and education to agriculture and sustainability. The hackathon's focus on real-world problems and its potential to drive positive change has made it a popular platform for students seeking to make a difference.

We would like to thank you for the immense response for the SIH 2024.

Moving ahead, The submission phase of ideas is now closed for the problem statements for which the idea count is more than 100. However, the portal is still open for entries for approx. 50 problem statements for which less ideas were less than 100.

In this regard, if your student has failed to nominate and submit the ideas, then this is the final call for idea submission against these problem statements (attached list of PS).

Also, we have added option to nominate 10 more new teams as wild card entries from each institute who had registered on SIH 2024 portal and submit ideas against these 50 PSs.

Thus, we request you to please circulate this information with your student teams and potential new students teams that are interested to nominate and submit ideas against these 50 challenges.

The idea submission against these 50 PS will be open till 7th Oct 2024 and ideas can be submitted by either the already registered teams or new 10 teams (wild card) that can be nominated by the institute. Please note that the each team can submit ideas only against 2 problem statements and in case your registered teams have already nominated ideas against 2 different PS then they wont be able to submit ideas against these 50 PS. Ideas can be submitted by teams that have either:

A.      Team have not submitted any ideas in any of the PS
B.      Or Team has submitted only one idea on SIH portal
C.       Or New 10 wild card teams can submit 2 Ideas against any 2 PS (approx. 50 PS listed on SIH portal).

We would like your students to ensure maximum participation and idea submission against these 50 PS and thus likely increasing chances for selection for SIH 2024 (based on idea quality).

18/10/24, 5:57 pm - +91 92947 63061: Dear Academic Partner,

Here's a list of common issues faced on the TCS Codevita platform along with their resolutions. Kindly share with the candidates for smooth Participation.

1. Account Locked  
Issue: Account is locked, and unable to log in.  
Resolution: Send an email to campuscommune@tcs.com requesting to unlock your account. Be sure to include your username and registered email ID.

2. OTP(SMS) Sending Failed / Cannot Validate Phone Number  
Issue: Unable to receive OTP via SMS or validate your phone number.  
Resolution: Email campuscommune@tcs.com with your username, registered email ID, and a screenshot of the issue.

3. Invalid OTC(Authenticator Account)
Issue: OTC is not being accepted.  
Resolution: Ensure your device’s date and time are correctly synced. If the issue persists, reset your Authenticator account via this link: https://codevita.tcsapps.com/blogs/DeleteOTPAccount.jsp.

4. Reset Credentials  
Issue: Need to reset login Authenticator account.  
Resolution: Follow the instructions provided in this blog to reset your Authenticator account: https://codevita.tcsapps.com/blogs/DeleteOTPAccount.jsp.

5. CT/DT Reference Already Linked with a Different Account  
Issue: CT/DT reference number is linked to another account.  
Resolution: If you have access to the old account, delete the CT/DT number from it and add it to your new account. Alternatively, continue using the old account. Ideally, you should only create one account for Codevita.

6. University Name Not in the Dropdown  
Issue: University/Institute is not listed in the dropdown options.  
Resolution: Choose the "Others" option from the institute dropdown list.

7. Used Different Email ID in Codevita Registration and NextStep Registration  
Issue: Email IDs for Codevita and NextStep registrations do not match.  
Resolution: Although it is ideal to use the same email ID for both, you can still participate in Codevita using a different email ID than what is on your NextStep account.

4. *Internshala* - Focused on internships across various domains, including development and marketing.  
   Website: [https://internshala.com](https://internshala.com)

   Website: [https://mlh.io](https://mlh.io)

8. *GitHub Jobs* - Explore tech-related job and internship opportunities.  
   Website: [https://jobs.github.com](https://jobs.github.com)

   Website: [https://www.indeed.com](https://www.indeed.com)

29/03/25, 1:03 pm - +91 92947 63061: BlueQubit x Yale University Hackathon Incoming! 🧠⚛️

Excited to share that BlueQubit is teaming up with Yale University to host an in person + virtual quantum hackathon this April 12th 💻

The challenge will be based on peaked circuits, an idea originally proposed by Prof. Scott Aaronson—who will also be awarding prizes to the top teams 🏆
Here’s the setup:

 1️⃣ You’ll get a quantum circuit that encodes a hidden message
 2️⃣ You’ll have 24 hours to figure out what's the message

This is a fun and unique opportunity for quantum engineers, researchers, and enthusiasts to get hands-on with new ideas and push the boundaries of what today’s quantum tools can do 🚀

Registration closes soon: https://lnkd.in/dCREfxTe

We’re looking forward to connecting with the community and seeing what you all come up with!

In 2025, the program will focus on Cyber Security and Networking as key skill areas.
Eligible participants include Cisco Networking Academy students currently enrolled in 1st, 2nd, and 3rd year technical degree programs (e.g., B.Tech, BCA, BSc in IT/CS, MCA, MSc in IT/CS) and technical diploma students in their 1st or 2nd year. The registration process remains consistent with previous editions.

Internship Registration End: 31st May 2025.

Internship Duration: 8-10 Weeks.

Internship Pathway: Cybersecurity & Networking

22/04/25, 11:22 am - +91 92947 63061: CISCO VIRTUAL INTERNSHIPS PROGRAM 2025
 	
We are thrilled to announce the launch of the VIP 2025, following the tremendous success of our previous virtual internship programs, which provided over 232,000 opportunities in Cyber Security and Networking.

In our ongoing commitment to prioritize skill development and bolster India's position as a digital talent hub, Cisco and the All India Council for Technical Education (AICTE) and NASSCOM have partnered to launch the latest phase of our virtual internship program.

This initiative aims to offer virtual internships in as per below mentioned pathways through the Cisco Networking Academy. This collaboration between industry and government is tailored to cultivate a skilled talent pool for the technology sector, aligning with the nation's digital skilling agenda.

Cyber Security Pathway: Introduction to Cybersecurity, Cybersecurity Essentials, Introduction to Packet Tracer
Networking Pathway: Networking Essentials, Introduction to Packet Tracer
 
The VIP represents a revolutionary shift towards virtualizing the traditional internship model, enabling scalability amidst challenging circumstances. 
 	
Student Registration Process
Step 1.   Register on the AICTE portal. (https://internship.aicte-india.org/register_new.php)
Step 2.  Apply for the Cisco Virtual Internship 2025.(https://internship.aicte-india.org/internship-details.php?uid=SU5URVJOU0hJUF8xNjU1MTkyNjk0NjBlMjc2YjM0NTM3NQ==)
Step 3.   Fill out the form for program access and training delivery. The NIIT Foundation team will guide and help to complete the NetAcad programs required for internship. (https://forms.gle/pc9i3kYM3kwJwnpx5)
Step 4.   Participate in the Cisco Industry session. (Session details will be communicated via email once released by Cisco to eligible students)
Step 5.   Students are required to upload their program certificate. (Upload Link will be shared after the Industry session via Email).
Step 6.   Students must upload their project work. (Upload Link will be shared after Industry session via Email).
Step 7.   The Virtual Internship certificate will be distributed to the college point of contact.

 	
Eligibility Criteria:

In 2025, the program will focus on Cyber Security and Networking as key skill areas.
Eligible participants include Cisco Networking Academy students currently enrolled in 1st, 2nd, and 3rd year technical degree programs (e.g., B.Tech, BCA, BSc in IT/CS, MCA, MSc in IT/CS) and technical diploma students in their 1st or 2nd year. The registration process remains consistent with previous editions.

Internship Registration Starts: 21st April 2025. 
Internship Registration End: 31st May 2025.

Internship Duration: 8-10 Weeks.

Internship Pathway: Cybersecurity & Networking
 	
Key Highlights of the Program:

Comprehensive curriculum covering core Cybersecurity and Networking concepts and applications.

☀️1️⃣ *What companies want now* 

IT companies in 2025–2026 are aggressively hiring for AI-driven and cloud-native roles.
The most in-demand technologies are:

Artificial Intelligence, Machine Learning, Deep Learning, Generative AI

Data Science, Data Engineering, Big Data (Spark, Hadoop, Kafka)

Cloud Platforms (AWS, Azure, Google Cloud)

DevOps / CI-CD / Automation Tools (Terraform, Ansible, Jenkins)

Cybersecurity / Cloud Security

Microservices & API-first architecture

IoT, Edge Computing, Real-time Streaming

Quantum Computing (early stage, but growing fast)


💡 In short:

> “AI + Cloud + Data + Automation” is the core skill combo companies now want.




---

☀️ 2️⃣ What a B.Tech CSE student should learn (2026 roadmap)

If you’re a CSE student aiming for a strong IT career, you need to build a hybrid skill set that mixes fundamentals + trending tech.

🎯 Strategy

1. Master the basics: Programming (Python, Java, C++), Data Structures, Algorithms.


2. Pick a strong stack: Example – Cloud + Machine Learning + DevOps.


3. Learn by projects: Make real projects on GitHub, do internships, open-source work.


4. Keep learning: Tech changes every 6 months — stay updated.


5. Develop soft skills: Communication, teamwork, adaptability, critical thinking.


6. Choose a niche: e.g. AI Security, MLOps, Cloud-native apps — less competition, higher demand.


☀️ 3️⃣ *Who got laid off — and why*

The employees being laid off are mostly mid-level and senior professionals or those with outdated skills.
They’re not “bad” employees — they just didn’t evolve with the new tech demand

👉 So, layoffs are not because they were lazy — it’s because the industry changed faster than their skills.

29/10/25, 2:57 pm - +91 99263 13942: श्रीराम ग्रुप, जबलपुर
सूचना / NOTICE

सभी विद्यार्थियों को सूचित किया जाता है कि छात्रवृत्ति (Scholarship) से संबंधित किसी भी प्रकार की कॉल आने या धनराशि (पैसे) की माँग किए जाने की स्थिति में तुरंत कॉलेज के संबंधित अधिकारी (Concern Authorities) से संपर्क करें।

साथ ही, अपनी छात्रवृत्ति से संबंधित किसी भी प्रकार की जानकारी या डेटा की पुष्टि हेतु कॉलेज में उपस्थित होकर ही संबंधित छात्रवृत्ति अधिकारी से संपर्क करें।

ध्यान दें कि किसी भी प्रकार की शुल्क (Fee) का भुगतान केवल “College Vidyalay App” अथवा कॉलेज द्वारा निर्धारित अधिकृत QR कोड या डिमांड ड्राफ्ट (DD) के माध्यम से ही मान्य होगा।

इनके अतिरिक्त किसी भी माध्यम से किया गया भुगतान कॉलेज द्वारा मान्य नहीं होगा।

RGPV – CS-503(B) | 
Total Unique Questions: 72
________________________________________
UNIT 1 – INTRODUCTION
1. Basic Concepts
1.	What is pattern recognition? Explain.
2.	What are the different components of a learning system?
3.	What is pattern classification? What are major paradigms of machine learning?
2. Learning Types
4.	Differentiate between supervised learning and unsupervised learning with suitable examples.
5.	Differentiate learning and adaptation.
6.	Why is pattern recognition important in machine learning?
3. Unsupervised Learning
7.	Discuss any unsupervised learning algorithm with an example.
8.	Define clustering and explain its importance in unsupervised learning.
4. Design Principles
9.	Explain various design principles of pattern recognition systems.
5. Probability & Statistics
10.	Define the law of total probability.
11.	What do you mean by normal distribution?
12.	Discuss mean and covariance with an example.
________________________________________
UNIT 2 – CLASSIFICATION
1. K-Nearest Neighbour (k-NN)
13.	How does the k-nearest neighbour method work?
14.	Explain KNN estimation and KNN rule.
15.	Write an algorithm for k-nearest neighbour estimation.
16.	Describe the k-Nearest Neighbors (k-NN) algorithm and its role in classification.
2. Classifier Concepts
17.	Write the difference between classification and clustering.
18.	How do we evaluate the performance of a classifier?
19.	What is a discriminant function? Explain its purpose.
20.	Define probabilistic classifiers and explain why they are useful in uncertain environments.
21.	What are rule-based classifiers? How do they derive rules from data?
3. Naïve Bayes & Related
22.	When is Naive Bayes particularly useful, and what are its limitations?
4. Random Forest
23.	Write a detailed note on Random Forest.
5. SVM
24.	Compare Support Vector Machine (SVM) and Relevance Vector Machine (RVM).
25.	In SVM, what does the hyperplane represent?
________________________________________
UNIT 3 – PATTERN RECOGNITION PARADIGMS
1. Paradigms Overview
26.	State and explain the different paradigms of pattern recognition.
27.	Show the differences between statistical and structural approaches.
2. Clustering Techniques
28.	Enlist clustering techniques and explain any one.
29.	What do you mean by hierarchical clustering? Explain.
30.	What is divisive hierarchical clustering? How is it different from agglomerative?
31.	Compare Grid-based methods with Density-based methods.
32.	Describe cluster validation.
3. Statistical Methods
33.	Explain chi-square test in detail.
34.	Describe similarity measures and their role in clustering and classification.
4. PCA & Dimension Reduction
35.	Discuss Principle Component Analysis (PCA) algorithm for dimension reduction.
36.	What is dimension reduction? Explain.
________________________________________
UNIT 4 – FEATURE EXTRACTION & SELECTION
1. Feature Extraction
37.	Discuss the various types of feature extraction.
38.	What is feature selection, and why is it important in pattern recognition?
2. Feature Selection Algorithms
39.	Illustrate branch and bound algorithm with suitable example.
40.	Write an algorithm for forward selection with suitable example.
3. Short Notes on Feature Measures
41.	Information gain
42.	Fisher’s score
43.	Correlation coefficient
44.	Variance threshold
45.	Mean absolute deviation
46.	Dispersion coefficient
________________________________________
UNIT 5 – RECENT ADVANCES IN PATTERN RECOGNITION
1. Fuzzy Logic & Neuro-Fuzzy
47.	Describe Neuro-Fuzzy systems and their techniques.
48.	Why use fuzzy classes? What is the fuzzy classification process?
49.	What do you mean by fuzzy decision-making?
2. Density Estimation
50.	Explain Parzen window and density estimation.
51.	Write a short note on Gaussian Mixture Model.
52.	Explain the concept of Gaussian Mixture Model. (Alternate phrasing)
3. HMM
53.	Explain the concept of Hidden Markov Model (HMM).
54.	Define HMM and list its three fundamental problems.
4. Neural Networks
55.	State Hebb’s rule.
56.	What is the role of the activation function in backpropagation?
57.	Neural network-based algorithms – explain.
58.	What happens when the learning rate is too high in backpropagation?

RGPV – CS-503(B) | 
Total Unique Questions: 72
________________________________________
UNIT 1 – INTRODUCTION
1. Basic Concepts
1.	What is pattern recognition? Explain.
2.	What are the different components of a learning system?
3.	What is pattern classification? What are major paradigms of machine learning?
2. Learning Types
4.	Differentiate between supervised learning and unsupervised learning with suitable examples.
5.	Differentiate learning and adaptation.
6.	Why is pattern recognition important in machine learning?
3. Unsupervised Learning
7.	Discuss any unsupervised learning algorithm with an example.
8.	Define clustering and explain its importance in unsupervised learning.
4. Design Principles
9.	Explain various design principles of pattern recognition systems.
5. Probability & Statistics
10.	Define the law of total probability.
11.	What do you mean by normal distribution?
12.	Discuss mean and covariance with an example.
________________________________________
UNIT 2 – CLASSIFICATION
1. K-Nearest Neighbour (k-NN)
13.	How does the k-nearest neighbour method work?
14.	Explain KNN estimation and KNN rule.
15.	Write an algorithm for k-nearest neighbour estimation.
16.	Describe the k-Nearest Neighbors (k-NN) algorithm and its role in classification.
2. Classifier Concepts
17.	Write the difference between classification and clustering.
18.	How do we evaluate the performance of a classifier?
19.	What is a discriminant function? Explain its purpose.
20.	Define probabilistic classifiers and explain why they are useful in uncertain environments.
21.	What are rule-based classifiers? How do they derive rules from data?
3. Naïve Bayes & Related
22.	When is Naive Bayes particularly useful, and what are its limitations?
4. Random Forest
23.	Write a detailed note on Random Forest.
5. SVM
24.	Compare Support Vector Machine (SVM) and Relevance Vector Machine (RVM).
25.	In SVM, what does the hyperplane represent?
________________________________________
UNIT 3 – PATTERN RECOGNITION PARADIGMS
1. Paradigms Overview
26.	State and explain the different paradigms of pattern recognition.
27.	Show the differences between statistical and structural approaches.
2. Clustering Techniques
28.	Enlist clustering techniques and explain any one.
29.	What do you mean by hierarchical clustering? Explain.
30.	What is divisive hierarchical clustering? How is it different from agglomerative?
31.	Compare Grid-based methods with Density-based methods.
32.	Describe cluster validation.
3. Statistical Methods
33.	Explain chi-square test in detail.
34.	Describe similarity measures and their role in clustering and classification.
4. PCA & Dimension Reduction
35.	Discuss Principle Component Analysis (PCA) algorithm for dimension reduction.
36.	What is dimension reduction? Explain.
________________________________________
UNIT 4 – FEATURE EXTRACTION & SELECTION
1. Feature Extraction
37.	Discuss the various types of feature extraction.
38.	What is feature selection, and why is it important in pattern recognition?
2. Feature Selection Algorithms
39.	Illustrate branch and bound algorithm with suitable example.
40.	Write an algorithm for forward selection with suitable example.
3. Short Notes on Feature Measures
41.	Information gain
42.	Fisher’s score
43.	Correlation coefficient
44.	Variance threshold
45.	Mean absolute deviation
46.	Dispersion coefficient
________________________________________
UNIT 5 – RECENT ADVANCES IN PATTERN RECOGNITION
1. Fuzzy Logic & Neuro-Fuzzy

48.	Why use fuzzy classes? What is the fuzzy classification process?
49.	What do you mean by fuzzy decision-making?
2. Density Estimation
50.	Explain Parzen window and density estimation.
51.	Write a short note on Gaussian Mixture Model.
52.	Explain the concept of Gaussian Mixture Model. (Alternate phrasing)
3. HMM

54.	Define HMM and list its three fundamental problems.
